{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_015EEp6Nk47bJkQugYJ65m4r","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: # gRPCurl\\n2: [![Build Status](https://circleci.com/gh/fullstorydev/grpcurl/tree/master.svg?style=svg)](https://circleci.com/gh/fullstorydev/grpcurl/tree/master)\\n3: [![Go Report Card](https://goreportcard.com/badge/github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl)](https://goreportcard.com/report/github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl)\\n4: \\n5: `grpcurl` is a command-line tool that lets you interact with gRPC servers. It's\\n6: basically `curl` for gRPC servers.\\n7: \\n8: The main purpose for this tool is to invoke RPC methods on a gRPC server from the\\n9: command-line. gRPC servers use a binary encoding on the wire\\n10: ([protocol buffers](https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers/), or \\\"protobufs\\\"\\n11: for short). So they are basically impossible to interact with using regular `curl`\\n12: (and older versions of `curl` that do not support HTTP/2 are of course non-starters).\\n13: This program accepts messages using JSON encoding, which is much more friendly for both\\n14: humans and scripts.\\n15: \\n16: With this tool you can also browse the schema for gRPC services, either by querying\\n17: a server that supports [server reflection](https://github.com/grpc/grpc/blob/master/src/proto/grpc/reflection/v1alpha/reflection.proto),\\n18: by reading proto source files, or by loading in compiled \\\"protoset\\\" files (files that contain\\n19: encoded file [descriptor protos](https://github.com/google/protobuf/blob/master/src/google/protobuf/descriptor.proto)).\\n20: In fact, the way the tool transforms JSON request data into a binary encoded protobuf\\n21: is using that very same schema. So, if the server you interact with does not support\\n22: reflection, you will either need the proto source files that define the service or need\\n23: protoset files that `grpcurl` can use.\\n24: \\n25: This repo also provides a library package, `github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl`, that has\\n26: functions for simplifying the construction of other command-line tools that dynamically\\n27: invoke gRPC endpoints. This code is a great example of how to use the various packages of\\n28: the [protoreflect](https://godoc.org/github.com/jhump/protoreflect) library, and shows\\n29: off what they can do.\\n30: \\n31: See also the [`grpcurl` talk at GopherCon 2018](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dDr-8kbMnaw).\\n32: \\n33: ## Features\\n34: `grpcurl` supports all kinds of RPC methods, including streaming methods. You can even\\n35: operate bi-directional streaming methods interactively by running `grpcurl` from an\\n36: interactive terminal and using stdin as the request body!\\n37: \\n38: `grpcurl` supports both secure/TLS servers _and_ plain-text servers (i.e. no TLS) and has\\n39: numerous options for TLS configuration. It also supports mutual TLS, where the client is\\n40: required to present a client certificate.\\n41: \\n42: As mentioned above, `grpcurl` works seamlessly if the server supports the reflection\\n43: service. If not, you can supply the `.proto` source files or you can supply protoset\\n44: files (containing compiled descriptors, produced by `protoc`) to `grpcurl`.\\n45: \\n46: ## Installation\\n47: \\n48: ### Binaries\\n49: \\n50: Download the binary from the [releases](https://github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl/releases) page.\\n51: \\n52: ### Homebrew (macOS)\\n53: \\n54: On macOS, `grpcurl` is available via Homebrew:\\n55: ```shell\\n56: brew install grpcurl\\n57: ```\\n58: \\n59: ### Docker\\n60: \\n61: For platforms that support Docker, you can download an image that lets you run `grpcurl`:\\n62: ```shell\\n63: # Download image\\n64: docker pull fullstorydev/grpcurl:latest\\n65: # Run the tool\\n66: docker run fullstorydev/grpcurl api.grpc.me:443 list\\n67: ```\\n68: Note that there are some pitfalls when using docker:\\n69: - If you need to interact with a server listening on the host's loopback network, you must specify the host as `host.docker.internal` instead of `localhost` (for Mac or Windows) _OR_ have the container use the host network with `-network=\\\"host\\\"` (Linux only).\\n70: - If you need to provide proto source files or descriptor sets, you must mount the folder containing the files as a volume (`-v $(pwd):/protos`) and adjust the import paths to container paths accordingly.\\n71: - If you want to provide the request message via stdin, using the `-d @` option, you need to use the `-i` flag on the docker command.\\n72: \\n73: ### Other Packages\\n74: \\n75: There are numerous other ways to install `grpcurl`, thanks to support from third parties that\\n76: have created recipes/packages for it. These include other ways to install `grpcurl` on a variety\\n77: of environments, including Windows and myriad Linux distributions.\\n78: \\n79: You can see more details and the full list of other packages for `grpcurl` at _repology.org_:\\n80: https://repology.org/project/grpcurl/information\\n81: \\n82: ### From Source\\n83: If you already have the [Go SDK](https://golang.org/doc/install) installed, you can use the `go`\\n84: tool to install `grpcurl`:\\n85: ```shell\\n86: go install github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl/cmd/grpcurl@latest\\n87: ```\\n88: \\n89: This installs the command into the `bin` sub-folder of wherever your `$GOPATH`\\n90: environment variable points. (If you have no `GOPATH` environment variable set,\\n91: the default install location is `$HOME/go/bin`). If this directory is already in\\n92: your `$PATH`, then you should be good to go.\\n93: \\n94: If you have already pulled down this repo to a location that is not in your\\n95: `$GOPATH` and want to build from the sources, you can `cd` into the repo and then\\n96: run `make install`.\\n97: \\n98: If you encounter compile errors and are using a version of the Go SDK older than 1.13,\\n99: you could have out-dated versions of `grpcurl`'s dependencies. You can update the\\n100: dependencies by running `make updatedeps`. Or, if you are using Go 1.11 or 1.12, you\\n101: can add `GO111MODULE=on` as a prefix to the commands above, which will also build using\\n102: the right versions of dependencies (vs. whatever you may already have in your `GOPATH`).\\n103: \\n104: ## Usage\\n105: The usage doc for the tool explains the numerous options:\\n106: ```shell\\n107: grpcurl -help\\n108: ```\\n109: \\n110: In the sections below, you will find numerous examples demonstrating how to use\\n111: `grpcurl`.\\n112: \\n113: ### Invoking RPCs\\n114: Invoking an RPC on a trusted server (e.g. TLS without self-signed key or custom CA)\\n115: that requires no client certs and supports server reflection is the simplest thing to\\n116: do with `grpcurl`. This minimal invocation sends an empty request body:\\n117: ```shell\\n118: grpcurl grpc.server.com:443 my.custom.server.Service/Method\\n119: \\n120: # no TLS\\n121: grpcurl -plaintext grpc.server.com:80 my.custom.server.Service/Method\\n122: ```\\n123: \\n124: To send a non-empty request, use the `-d` argument. Note that all arguments must come\\n125: *before* the server address and method name:\\n126: ```shell\\n127: grpcurl -d '{\\\"id\\\": 1234, \\\"tags\\\": [\\\"foo\\\",\\\"bar\\\"]}' \\\\\\n128:     grpc.server.com:443 my.custom.server.Service/Method\\n129: ```\\n130: \\n131: As can be seen in the example, the supplied body must be in JSON format. The body will\\n132: be parsed and then transmitted to the server in the protobuf binary format.\\n133: \\n134: If you want to include `grpcurl` in a command pipeline, such as when using `jq` to\\n135: create a request body, you can use `-d @`, which tells `grpcurl` to read the actual\\n136: request body from stdin:\\n137: ```shell\\n138: grpcurl -d @ grpc.server.com:443 my.custom.server.Service/Method <<EOM\\n139: {\\n140:   \\\"id\\\": 1234,\\n141:   \\\"tags\\\": [\\n142:     \\\"foor\\\",\\n143:     \\\"bar\\\"\\n144:   ]\\n145: }\\n146: EOM\\n147: ```\\n148: \\n149: ### Listing Services\\n150: To list all services exposed by a server, use the \\\"list\\\" verb. When using `.proto` source\\n151: or protoset files instead of server reflection, this lists all services defined in the\\n152: source or protoset files.\\n153: ```shell\\n154: # Server supports reflection\\n155: grpcurl localhost:8787 list\\n156: \\n157: # Using compiled protoset files\\n158: grpcurl -protoset my-protos.bin list\\n159: \\n160: # Using proto sources\\n161: grpcurl -import-path ../protos -proto my-stuff.proto list\\n162: ```\\n163: \\n164: The \\\"list\\\" verb also lets you see all methods in a particular service:\\n165: ```shell\\n166: grpcurl localhost:8787 list my.custom.server.Service\\n167: ```\\n168: \\n169: ### Describing Elements\\n170: The \\\"describe\\\" verb will print the type of any symbol that the server knows about\\n171: or that is found in a given protoset file. It also prints a description of that\\n172: symbol, in the form of snippets of proto source. It won't necessarily be the\\n173: original source that defined the element, but it will be equivalent.\\n174: \\n175: ```shell\\n176: # Server supports reflection\\n177: grpcurl localhost:8787 describe my.custom.server.Service.MethodOne\\n178: \\n179: # Using compiled protoset files\\n180: grpcurl -protoset my-protos.bin describe my.custom.server.Service.MethodOne\\n181: \\n182: # Using proto sources\\n183: grpcurl -import-path ../protos -proto my-stuff.proto describe my.custom.server.Service.MethodOne\\n184: ```\\n185: \\n186: ## Descriptor Sources\\n187: The `grpcurl` tool can operate on a variety of sources for descriptors. The descriptors\\n188: are required, in order for `grpcurl` to understand the RPC schema, translate inputs\\n189: into the protobuf binary format as well as translate responses from the binary format\\n190: into text. The sections below document the supported sources and what command-line flags\\n191: are needed to use them.\\n192: \\n193: ### Server Reflection\\n194: \\n195: Without any additional command-line flags, `grpcurl` will try to use [server reflection](https://github.com/grpc/grpc/blob/master/src/proto/grpc/reflection/v1alpha/reflection.proto).\\n196: \\n197: Examples for how to set up server reflection can be found [here](https://github.com/grpc/grpc/blob/master/doc/server-reflection.md#known-implementations).\\n198: \\n199: When using reflection, the server address (host:port or path to Unix socket) is required\\n200: even for \\\"list\\\" and \\\"describe\\\" operations, so that `grpcurl` can connect to the server\\n201: and ask it for its descriptors.\\n202: \\n203: ### Proto Source Files\\n204: To use `grpcurl` on servers that do not support reflection, you can use `.proto` source\\n205: files.\\n206: \\n207: In addition to using `-proto` flags to point `grpcurl` at the relevant proto source file(s),\\n208: you may also need to supply `-import-path` flags to tell `grpcurl` the folders from which\\n209: dependencies can be imported.\\n210: \\n211: Just like when compiling with `protoc`, you do *not* need to provide an import path for the\\n212: location of the standard protos included with `protoc` (which contain various \\\"well-known\\n213: types\\\" with a package definition of `google.protobuf`). These files are \\\"known\\\" by `grpcurl`\\n214: as a snapshot of their descriptors is built into the `grpcurl` binary.\\n215: \\n216: When using proto sources, you can omit the server address (host:port or path to Unix socket)\\n217: when using the \\\"list\\\" and \\\"describe\\\" operations since they only need to consult the proto\\n218: source files.\\n219: \\n220: ### Protoset Files\\n221: You can also use compiled protoset files with `grpcurl`. If you are scripting `grpcurl` and\\n222: need to re-use the same proto sources for many invocations, you will see better performance\\n223: by using protoset files (since it skips the parsing and compilation steps with each\\n224: invocation).\\n225: \\n226: Protoset files contain binary encoded `google.protobuf.FileDescriptorSet` protos. To create\\n227: a protoset file, invoke `protoc` with the `*.proto` files that define the service:\\n228: ```shell\\n229: protoc --proto_path=. \\\\\\n230:     --descriptor_set_out=myservice.protoset \\\\\\n231:     --include_imports \\\\\\n232:     my/custom/server/service.proto\\n233: ```\\n234: \\n235: The `--descriptor_set_out` argument is what tells `protoc` to produce a protoset,\\n236: and the `--include_imports` argument is necessary for the protoset to contain\\n237: everything that `grpcurl` needs to process and understand the schema.\\n238: \\n239: When using protosets, you can omit the server address (host:port or path to Unix socket)\\n240: when using the \\\"list\\\" and \\\"describe\\\" operations since they only need to consult the\\n241: protoset files.\\n242: \\n243: \",\"url\":\"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/grpcurl--25c896aa@75c2b5d7e260014d5f01be91b47bbf0f4adddfc1/-/blob/README.md\"}"}]},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"ff0112dd-a1a1-4a99-8812-b78d30a328e3","uuid":"281aad2d-8699-47c6-b705-bdd5d77c4b66","tool_use_result":{"content":"{\"content\":\"1: # gRPCurl\\n2: [![Build Status](https://circleci.com/gh/fullstorydev/grpcurl/tree/master.svg?style=svg)](https://circleci.com/gh/fullstorydev/grpcurl/tree/master)\\n3: [![Go Report Card](https://goreportcard.com/badge/github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl)](https://goreportcard.com/report/github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl)\\n4: \\n5: `grpcurl` is a command-line tool that lets you interact with gRPC servers. It's\\n6: basically `curl` for gRPC servers.\\n7: \\n8: The main purpose for this tool is to invoke RPC methods on a gRPC server from the\\n9: command-line. gRPC servers use a binary encoding on the wire\\n10: ([protocol buffers](https://developers.google.com/protocol-buffers/), or \\\"protobufs\\\"\\n11: for short). So they are basically impossible to interact with using regular `curl`\\n12: (and older versions of `curl` that do not support HTTP/2 are of course non-starters).\\n13: This program accepts messages using JSON encoding, which is much more friendly for both\\n14: humans and scripts.\\n15: \\n16: With this tool you can also browse the schema for gRPC services, either by querying\\n17: a server that supports [server reflection](https://github.com/grpc/grpc/blob/master/src/proto/grpc/reflection/v1alpha/reflection.proto),\\n18: by reading proto source files, or by loading in compiled \\\"protoset\\\" files (files that contain\\n19: encoded file [descriptor protos](https://github.com/google/protobuf/blob/master/src/google/protobuf/descriptor.proto)).\\n20: In fact, the way the tool transforms JSON request data into a binary encoded protobuf\\n21: is using that very same schema. So, if the server you interact with does not support\\n22: reflection, you will either need the proto source files that define the service or need\\n23: protoset files that `grpcurl` can use.\\n24: \\n25: This repo also provides a library package, `github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl`, that has\\n26: functions for simplifying the construction of other command-line tools that dynamically\\n27: invoke gRPC endpoints. This code is a great example of how to use the various packages of\\n28: the [protoreflect](https://godoc.org/github.com/jhump/protoreflect) library, and shows\\n29: off what they can do.\\n30: \\n31: See also the [`grpcurl` talk at GopherCon 2018](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=dDr-8kbMnaw).\\n32: \\n33: ## Features\\n34: `grpcurl` supports all kinds of RPC methods, including streaming methods. You can even\\n35: operate bi-directional streaming methods interactively by running `grpcurl` from an\\n36: interactive terminal and using stdin as the request body!\\n37: \\n38: `grpcurl` supports both secure/TLS servers _and_ plain-text servers (i.e. no TLS) and has\\n39: numerous options for TLS configuration. It also supports mutual TLS, where the client is\\n40: required to present a client certificate.\\n41: \\n42: As mentioned above, `grpcurl` works seamlessly if the server supports the reflection\\n43: service. If not, you can supply the `.proto` source files or you can supply protoset\\n44: files (containing compiled descriptors, produced by `protoc`) to `grpcurl`.\\n45: \\n46: ## Installation\\n47: \\n48: ### Binaries\\n49: \\n50: Download the binary from the [releases](https://github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl/releases) page.\\n51: \\n52: ### Homebrew (macOS)\\n53: \\n54: On macOS, `grpcurl` is available via Homebrew:\\n55: ```shell\\n56: brew install grpcurl\\n57: ```\\n58: \\n59: ### Docker\\n60: \\n61: For platforms that support Docker, you can download an image that lets you run `grpcurl`:\\n62: ```shell\\n63: # Download image\\n64: docker pull fullstorydev/grpcurl:latest\\n65: # Run the tool\\n66: docker run fullstorydev/grpcurl api.grpc.me:443 list\\n67: ```\\n68: Note that there are some pitfalls when using docker:\\n69: - If you need to interact with a server listening on the host's loopback network, you must specify the host as `host.docker.internal` instead of `localhost` (for Mac or Windows) _OR_ have the container use the host network with `-network=\\\"host\\\"` (Linux only).\\n70: - If you need to provide proto source files or descriptor sets, you must mount the folder containing the files as a volume (`-v $(pwd):/protos`) and adjust the import paths to container paths accordingly.\\n71: - If you want to provide the request message via stdin, using the `-d @` option, you need to use the `-i` flag on the docker command.\\n72: \\n73: ### Other Packages\\n74: \\n75: There are numerous other ways to install `grpcurl`, thanks to support from third parties that\\n76: have created recipes/packages for it. You can even\n35: operate bi-directional streaming methods interactively by running `grpcurl` from an\n36: interactive terminal and using stdin as the request body!\n37: \n38: `grpcurl` supports both secure/TLS servers _and_ plain-text servers (i.e. no TLS) and has\n39: numerous options for TLS configuration. It also supports mutual TLS, where the client is\n40: required to present a client certificate.\n41: \n42: As mentioned above, `grpcurl` works seamlessly if the server supports the reflection\n43: service. If not, you can supply the `.proto` source files or you can supply protoset\n44: files (containing compiled descriptors, produced by `protoc`) to `grpcurl`.\n45: \n46: ## Installation\n47: \n48: ### Binaries\n49: \n50: Download the binary from the [releases](https://github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl/releases) page.\n51: \n52: ### Homebrew (macOS)\n53: \n54: On macOS, `grpcurl` is available via Homebrew:\n55: ```shell\n56: brew install grpcurl\n57: ```\n58: \n59: ### Docker\n60: \n61: For platforms that support Docker, you can download an image that lets you run `grpcurl`:\n62: ```shell\n63: # Download image\n64: docker pull fullstorydev/grpcurl:latest\n65: # Run the tool\n66: docker run fullstorydev/grpcurl api.grpc.me:443 list\n67: ```\n68: Note that there are some pitfalls when using docker:\n69: - If you need to interact with a server listening on the host's loopback network, you must specify the host as `host.docker.internal` instead of `localhost` (for Mac or Windows) _OR_ have the container use the host network with `-network=\"host\"` (Linux only).\n70: - If you need to provide proto source files or descriptor sets, you must mount the folder containing the files as a volume (`-v $(pwd):/protos`) and adjust the import paths to container paths accordingly.\n71: - If you want to provide the request message via stdin, using the `-d @` option, you need to use the `-i` flag on the docker command.\n72: \n73: ### Other Packages\n74: \n75: There are numerous other ways to install `grpcurl`, thanks to support from third parties that\n76: have created recipes/packages for it. These include other ways to install `grpcurl` on a variety\n77: of environments, including Windows and myriad Linux distributions.\n78: \n79: You can see more details and the full list of other packages for `grpcurl` at _repology.org_:\n80: https://repology.org/project/grpcurl/information\n81: \n82: ### From Source\n83: If you already have the [Go SDK](https://golang.org/doc/install) installed, you can use the `go`\n84: tool to install `grpcurl`:\n85: ```shell\n86: go install github.com/fullstorydev/grpcurl/cmd/grpcurl@latest\n87: ```\n88: \n89: This installs the command into the `bin` sub-folder of wherever your `$GOPATH`\n90: environment variable points. (If you have no `GOPATH` environment variable set,\n91: the default install location is `$HOME/go/bin`). If this directory is already in\n92: your `$PATH`, then you should be good to go.\n93: \n94: If you have already pulled down this repo to a location that is not in your\n95: `$GOPATH` and want to build from the sources, you can `cd` into the repo and then\n96: run `make install`.\n97: \n98: If you encounter compile errors and are using a version of the Go SDK older than 1.13,\n99: you could have out-dated versions of `grpcurl`'s dependencies. You can update the\n100: dependencies by running `make updatedeps`. Or, if you are using Go 1.11 or 1.12, you\n101: can add `GO111MODULE=on` as a prefix to the commands above, which will also build using\n102: the right versions of dependencies (vs. whatever you may already have in your `GOPATH`).\n103: \n104: ## Usage\n105: The usage doc for the tool explains the numerous options:\n106: ```shell\n107: grpcurl -help\n108: ```\n109: \n110: In the sections below, you will find numerous examples demonstrating how to use\n111: `grpcurl`.\n112: \n113: ### Invoking RPCs\n114: Invoking an RPC on a trusted server (e.g. TLS without self-signed key or custom CA)\n115: that requires no client certs and supports server reflection is the simplest thing to\n116: do with `grpcurl`. This minimal invocation sends an empty request body:\n117: ```shell\n118: grpcurl grpc.server.com:443 my.custom.server.Service/Method\n119: \n120: # no TLS\n121: grpcurl -plaintext grpc.server.com:80 my.custom.server.Service/Method\n122: ```\n123: \n124: To send a non-empty request, use the `-d` argument. Note that all arguments must come\n125: *before* the server address and method name:\n126: ```shell\n127: grpcurl -d '{\"id\": 1234, \"tags\": [\"foo\",\"bar\"]}' \\\n128:     grpc.server.com:443 my.custom.server.Service/Method\n129: ```\n130: \n131: As can be seen in the example, the supplied body must be in JSON format. The body will\n132: be parsed and then transmitted to the server in the protobuf binary format.\n133: \n134: If you want to include `grpcurl` in a command pipeline, such as when using `jq` to\n135: create a request body, you can use `-d @`, which tells `grpcurl` to read the actual\n136: request body from stdin:\n137: ```shell\n138: grpcurl -d @ grpc.server.com:443 my.custom.server.Service/Method <<EOM\n139: {\n140:   \"id\": 1234,\n141:   \"tags\": [\n142:     \"foor\",\n143:     \"bar\"\n144:   ]\n145: }\n146: EOM\n147: ```\n148: \n149: ### Listing Services\n150: To list all services exposed by a server, use the \"list\" verb. When using `.proto` source\n151: or protoset files instead of server reflection, this lists all services defined in the\n152: source or protoset files.\n153: ```shell\n154: # Server supports reflection\n155: grpcurl localhost:8787 list\n156: \n157: # Using compiled protoset files\n158: grpcurl -protoset my-protos.bin list\n159: \n160: # Using proto sources\n161: grpcurl -import-path ../protos -proto my-stuff.proto list\n162: ```\n163: \n164: The \"list\" verb also lets you see all methods in a particular service:\n165: ```shell\n166: grpcurl localhost:8787 list my.custom.server.Service\n167: ```\n168: \n169: ### Describing Elements\n170: The \"describe\" verb will print the type of any symbol that the server knows about\n171: or that is found in a given protoset file. It also prints a description of that\n172: symbol, in the form of snippets of proto source. It won't necessarily be the\n173: original source that defined the element, but it will be equivalent.\n174: \n175: ```shell\n176: # Server supports reflection\n177: grpcurl localhost:8787 describe my.custom.server.Service.MethodOne\n178: \n179: # Using compiled protoset files\n180: grpcurl -protoset my-protos.bin describe my.custom.server.Service.MethodOne\n181: \n182: # Using proto sources\n183: grpcurl -import-path ../protos -proto my-stuff.proto describe my.custom.server.Service.MethodOne\n184: ```\n185: \n186: ## Descriptor Sources\n187: The `grpcurl` tool can operate on a variety of sources for descriptors. The descriptors\n188: are required, in order for `grpcurl` to understand the RPC schema, translate inputs\n189: into the protobuf binary format as well as translate responses from the binary format\n190: into text. The sections below document the supported sources and what command-line flags\n191: are needed to use them.\n192: \n193: ### Server Reflection\n194: \n195: Without any additional command-line flags, `grpcurl` will try to use [server reflection](https://github.com/grpc/grpc/blob/master/src/proto/grpc/reflection/v1alpha/reflection.proto).\n196: \n197: Examples for how to set up server reflection can be found [here](https://github.com/grpc/grpc/blob/master/doc/server-reflection.md#known-implementations).\n198: \n199: When using reflection, the server address (host:port or path to Unix socket) is required\n200: even for \"list\" and \"describe\" operations, so that `grpcurl` can connect to the server\n201: and ask it for its descriptors.\n202: \n203: ### Proto Source Files\n204: To use `grpcurl` on servers that do not support reflection, you can use `.proto` source\n205: files.\n206: \n207: In addition to using `-proto` flags to point `grpcurl` at the relevant proto source file(s),\n208: you may also need to supply `-import-path` flags to tell `grpcurl` the folders from which\n209: dependencies can be imported.\n210: \n211: Just like when compiling with `protoc`, you do *not* need to provide an import path for the\n212: location of the standard protos included with `protoc` (which contain various \"well-known\n213: types\" with a package definition of `google.protobuf`). These files are \"known\" by `grpcurl`\n214: as a snapshot of their descriptors is built into the `grpcurl` binary.\n215: \n216: When using proto sources, you can omit the server address (host:port or path to Unix socket)\n217: when using the \"list\" and \"describe\" operations since they only need to consult the proto\n218: source files.\n219: \n220: ### Protoset Files\n221: You can also use compiled protoset files with `grpcurl`. If you are scripting `grpcurl` and\n222: need to re-use the same proto sources for many invocations, you will see better performance\n223: by using protoset files (since it skips the parsing and compilation steps with each\n224: invocation).\n225: \n226: Protoset files contain binary encoded `google.protobuf.FileDescriptorSet` protos. To create\n227: a protoset file, invoke `protoc` with the `*.proto` files that define the service:\n228: ```shell\n229: protoc --proto_path=. \\\n230:     --descriptor_set_out=myservice.protoset \\\n231:     --include_imports \\\n232:     my/custom/server/service.proto\n233: ```\n234: \n235: The `--descriptor_set_out` argument is what tells `protoc` to produce a protoset,\n236: and the `--include_imports` argument is necessary for the protoset to contain\n237: everything that `grpcurl` needs to process and understand the schema.\n238: \n239: When using protosets, you can omit the server address (host:port or path to Unix socket)\n240: when using the \"list\" and \"describe\" operations since they only need to consult the\n241: protoset files.\n242: \n243: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/grpcurl--25c896aa@75c2b5d7e260014d5f01be91b47bbf0f4adddfc1/-/blob/README.md"}}}

It's basically curl for gRPC servers.\"\n\n**Assessment:** ✅ grpcurl is exclusively a **CLIENT** tool\n\n### HTTP/2 Server Usage in grpcurl\n\n**Search for `grpc.Server` usage in grpcurl:**\n\nResults show `grpc.Server` only in:\n1. **Test files** (`tls_settings_test.go`) - internal testing infrastructure, not production code\n2. **Generated protobuf files** (`test.pb.go`, `bank.pb.go`) - just server registration function signatures\n3. **Test/demo servers** (`testserver/testserver.go`, `bankdemo/main.go`) - these are standalone test servers, separate binaries from grpcurl\n\n**Primary grpcurl code:** No usage of grpc.Server\n\n**Assessment:** ✅ grpcurl does NOT run any HTTP/2 servers\n\n### HTTP/2 Client Usage in grpcurl\n\n**grpcurl Usage Pattern:**\n1. Accepts user input (gRPC method, server address, request data)\n2. Creates a **client connection** to the target gRPC server\n3. Invokes RPC methods on that server\n4. Displays responses\n\n**Assessment:** ✅ grpcurl exclusively uses HTTP/2 **client** functionality via grpc-go's http2Client\n\n### Vulnerable Function Path\n\n**Vulnerable Function:** `golang.org/x/net/http2.Server.ServeConn()`\n\n**Type:** **SERVER** function\n\n**Trigger:** Accepts incoming HTTP/2 connections and processes frames\n\n**grpcurl Usage:** ❌ NEVER CALLED\n\ngrpcurl never instantiates or calls `http2.Server.ServeConn()` because it never runs an HTTP/2 server.\n\n---\n\n## Impact Assessment\n\n### Affected: **NO**\n\n**Rationale:**\n\nCVE-2023-39325 is a **server-side vulnerability** in the HTTP/2 protocol implementation. Specifically, it allows a malicious HTTP/2 **client** to cause excessive resource consumption on an HTTP/2 **server** by:\n\n1. Rapidly creating requests\n2. Immediately resetting them with RST_STREAM frames\n3. Creating new requests while old ones are still executing\n\n**grpcurl is a client tool** and never runs an HTTP/2 server. Therefore, it cannot be exploited by this vulnerability. The attack vector requires:\n- An HTTP/2 server accepting connections\n- Ability to send malicious RST_STREAM frames to the server\n- Server processing of requests/streams\n\nNone of these conditions apply to grpcurl.\n\n### Risk Level: **NONE**\n\n**Exploitability:** An attacker **cannot** trigger CVE-2023-39325 against grpcurl because:\n\n1. grpcurl never creates an HTTP/2 server\n2. No server connection listeners exist\n3. grpcurl never accepts incoming connections\n4. The vulnerable `http2.Server.ServeConn()` is never called by grpcurl\n\n### Dependency Status\n\nWhile grpcurl transitively depends on golang.org/x/net v0.9.0, this is analogous to a client having a vulnerable library installed locally. The vulnerability is only exposed if the client:\n- Runs an HTTP/2 server\n- Accepts connections from untrusted sources\n\ngrpcurl does neither.\n\n---\n\n## Remediation\n\n**Recommended Actions:** **No action required**\n\nWhile a best-practice approach would be to upgrade dependencies, grpcurl is **not at risk** from CVE-2023-39325, so this upgrade is not a security necessity for this specific vulnerability.\n\n**However, if grpc-go is upgraded to a version that depends on golang.org/x/net >= v0.17.0, grpcurl would benefit from:**\n- Improved security posture (dependency hygiene)\n- Access to bug fixes and performance improvements in the newer golang.org/x/net version\n- Better alignment with security best practices\n\n---\n\n## Summary Table\n\n| Aspect | Finding |\n|--------|---------|\n| **Vulnerable Package** | golang.org/x/net v0.9.0 |\n| **Vulnerable Function** | http2.Server.ServeConn() |\n| **Vulnerability Type** | Server-side DoS via HTTP/2 Rapid Reset |\n| **Direct Dependency** | grpcurl → grpc-go ✅ |\n| **Transitive Dependency** | grpc-go → golang.org/x/net v0.9.0 ✅ |\n| **Grpcurl Architecture** | Client-only tool |\n| **Server Functionality Used** | None |\n| **Vulnerable Code Path Used** | No |\n| **Affected by CVE-2023-39325** | **NO** |\n| **Risk Level** | **NONE** |\n| **Remediation Required** | No |\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":10,"cache_creation_input_tokens":5458,"cache_read_input_tokens":63333,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":5458},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"ff0112dd-a1a1-4a99-8812-b78d30a328e3","uuid":"297e80b0-528e-47db-8540-9b13412a7d13"}

It's basically curl for gRPC servers.\"\n\n**Assessment:** ✅ grpcurl is exclusively a **CLIENT** tool\n\n### HTTP/2 Server Usage in grpcurl\n\n**Search for `grpc.Server` usage in grpcurl:**\n\nResults show `grpc.Server` only in:\n1. **Test files** (`tls_settings_test.go`) - internal testing infrastructure, not production code\n2. **Generated protobuf files** (`test.pb.go`, `bank.pb.go`) - just server registration function signatures\n3. **Test/demo servers** (`testserver/testserver.go`, `bankdemo/main.go`) - these are standalone test servers, separate binaries from grpcurl\n\n**Primary grpcurl code:** No usage of grpc.Server\n\n**Assessment:** ✅ grpcurl does NOT run any HTTP/2 servers\n\n### HTTP/2 Client Usage in grpcurl\n\n**grpcurl Usage Pattern:**\n1. Accepts user input (gRPC method, server address, request data)\n2. Creates a **client connection** to the target gRPC server\n3. Invokes RPC methods on that server\n4. Displays responses\n\n**Assessment:** ✅ grpcurl exclusively uses HTTP/2 **client** functionality via grpc-go's http2Client\n\n### Vulnerable Function Path\n\n**Vulnerable Function:** `golang.org/x/net/http2.Server.ServeConn()`\n\n**Type:** **SERVER** function\n\n**Trigger:** Accepts incoming HTTP/2 connections and processes frames\n\n**grpcurl Usage:** ❌ NEVER CALLED\n\ngrpcurl never instantiates or calls `http2.Server.ServeConn()` because it never runs an HTTP/2 server.\n\n---\n\n## Impact Assessment\n\n### Affected: **NO**\n\n**Rationale:**\n\nCVE-2023-39325 is a **server-side vulnerability** in the HTTP/2 protocol implementation. Specifically, it allows a malicious HTTP/2 **client** to cause excessive resource consumption on an HTTP/2 **server** by:\n\n1. Rapidly creating requests\n2. Immediately resetting them with RST_STREAM frames\n3. Creating new requests while old ones are still executing\n\n**grpcurl is a client tool** and never runs an HTTP/2 server. Therefore, it cannot be exploited by this vulnerability. The attack vector requires:\n- An HTTP/2 server accepting connections\n- Ability to send malicious RST_STREAM frames to the server\n- Server processing of requests/streams\n\nNone of these conditions apply to grpcurl.\n\n### Risk Level: **NONE**\n\n**Exploitability:** An attacker **cannot** trigger CVE-2023-39325 against grpcurl because:\n\n1. grpcurl never creates an HTTP/2 server\n2. No server connection listeners exist\n3. grpcurl never accepts incoming connections\n4. The vulnerable `http2.Server.ServeConn()` is never called by grpcurl\n\n### Dependency Status\n\nWhile grpcurl transitively depends on golang.org/x/net v0.9.0, this is analogous to a client having a vulnerable library installed locally. The vulnerability is only exposed if the client:\n- Runs an HTTP/2 server\n- Accepts connections from untrusted sources\n\ngrpcurl does neither.\n\n---\n\n## Remediation\n\n**Recommended Actions:** **No action required**\n\nWhile a best-practice approach would be to upgrade dependencies, grpcurl is **not at risk** from CVE-2023-39325, so this upgrade is not a security necessity for this specific vulnerability.\n\n**However, if grpc-go is upgraded to a version that depends on golang.org/x/net >= v0.17.0, grpcurl would benefit from:**\n- Improved security posture (dependency hygiene)\n- Access to bug fixes and performance improvements in the newer golang.org/x/net version\n- Better alignment with security best practices\n\n---\n\n## Summary Table\n\n| Aspect | Finding |\n|--------|---------|\n| **Vulnerable Package** | golang.org/x/net v0.9.0 |\n| **Vulnerable Function** | http2.Server.ServeConn() |\n| **Vulnerability Type** | Server-side DoS via HTTP/2 Rapid Reset |\n| **Direct Dependency** | grpcurl → grpc-go ✅ |\n| **Transitive Dependency** | grpc-go → golang.org/x/net v0.9.0 ✅ |\n| **Grpcurl Architecture** | Client-only tool |\n| **Server Functionality Used** | None |\n| **Vulnerable Code Path Used** | No |\n| **Affected by CVE-2023-39325** | **NO** |\n| **Risk Level** | **NONE** |\n| **Remediation Required** | No |\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
